    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>Service Type</h4><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>The pre-existing directory service type to which to bind TrueNAS. Select ACTIVEDIRECTORY to join an Active     Directory domain. Select IPA to join a FreeIPA domain. Select LDAP to bind to one or more OpenLDAP-compatible     servers. </p>

    <div class="card">
    <div class="card-header" id="headingCall_parameters_items_i0_credential">
    <h2 class="mb-0">
    <button aria-controls="Call_parameters_items_i0_credential" aria-expanded="" class="btn btn-link property-name-button" data-target="#Call_parameters_items_i0_credential" data-toggle="collapse" onclick="setAnchor('#Call_parameters_items_i0_credential')" type="button"><span class="property-name">credential</span></button>
    </h2>
    </div>
    <div aria-labelledby="headingCall_parameters_items_i0_credential" class="collapse property-definition-div" data-parent="#accordionCall_parameters_items_i0_credential" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_credential">
    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>Credential</h4><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>Credential used to bind to the specified directory service. Kerberos credentials are required for Active     Directory or IPA domains. Generic LDAP environments support various authentication methods. Available methods     depend on the remote LDAP server configuration. If Kerberos credentials are selected for LDAP, GSSAPI binds     replace plain LDAP binds. Use Kerberos or mutual TLS authentication when possible for better security.</p>
    <p>The following credential types are supported based on <code>service_type</code>:</p>
    <p><code>ACTIVEDIRECTORY</code> service_type: <code>KERBEROS_USER</code> and <code>KERBEROS_PRINCIPAL</code>.</p>
    <p><code>LDAP</code> service_type: <code>LDAP_PLAIN</code>, <code>LDAP_ANONYMOUS</code>, <code>LDAP_MTLS</code>, <code>KERBEROS_USER</code>, and <code>KERBEROS_PRINCIPAL</code>.     NOTE: prior configuration of kerberos realm is required in order to use kerberos credentials with the <code>LDAP</code> <code>service_type</code>.</p>
    <p><code>IPA</code> service_type: <code>KERBEROS_USER</code> and <code>KERBEROS_PRINCIPAL</code>. NOTE: <code>KERBEROS_USER</code> should be used when initially     joining an IPA domain. </p>
    </span><div class="any-of-value" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_credential_anyOf"><h2 class="handle">

    <h2 class="mb-0">
    <button aria-controls="Call_parameters_items_i0_enable" aria-expanded="" class="btn btn-link property-name-button" data-target="#Call_parameters_items_i0_enable" data-toggle="collapse" onclick="setAnchor('#Call_parameters_items_i0_enable')" type="button"><span class="property-name">enable</span></button>

    </div>
    <div aria-labelledby="headingCall_parameters_items_i0_enable" class="collapse property-definition-div" data-parent="#accordionCall_parameters_items_i0_enable" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_enable">
    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>Enable</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: boolean</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>Enable the directory service.</p>
    <p>If TrueNAS has never joined the specified domain (IPA or Active Directory), setting this to True causes TrueNAS to     attempt to join the domain.</p>
    <p>NOTE: The domain join process for Active Directory and IPA will make changes to the domain such as creating a new     computer account for the TrueNAS server and creating DNS records for TrueNAS. </p>
    </span>
    </div>
    </div>
    </div>
    </div>

    <h4>Enable Account Cache</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: boolean</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>Enable backend caching for user and group lists. If enabled, then directory services users and groups will be     presented as choices in the UI dropdowns and in API responses for user and group queries. This setting also     controls whether users and groups appear in getent results. Disable this setting to reduce load on the directory     server when necessary. </p>

        "sssd_compat": false
      }
    }</div></div><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>Configuration for mapping Active Directory accounts to accounts on the TrueNAS server.     <div class="card">
    <div class="card-header" id="headingCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain">
    <h2 class="mb-0">
    <button aria-controls="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain" aria-expanded="" class="btn btn-link property-name-button" data-target="#Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain" data-toggle="collapse" onclick="setAnchor('#Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain')" type="button"><span class="property-name">idmap_domain</span></button>
    </h2>
    </div>
    <div aria-labelledby="headingCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain" class="collapse property-definition-div" data-parent="#accordionCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain">
    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>Idmap Domain</h4> <div class="json-default-value">Default:<div class="value">{
      "name": null,
      "range_low": 100000001,
      "range_high": 200000000,
      "idmap_backend": "RID",
      "sssd_compat": false
    }</div></div><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>This configuration defines how domain accounts joined to TrueNAS are mapped to Unix UIDs and GIDs on the     TrueNAS server. Most TrueNAS deployments use the RID backend, which algorithmically assigns UIDs and GIDs based on     the Active Directory account SID. Another common option is the AD backend, which reads predefined Active Directory     LDAP schema attributes that assign explicit UID and GID numbers to accounts. </p>
    </span><div class="one-of-value" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf"><h2 class="handle">
    <label>One of</label>
    </h2><ul class="nav nav-tabs" id="tabsCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_oneOf" role="tablist"><li class="nav-item">
    <a class="nav-link active oneOf-option" data-toggle="tab" href="#tab-pane_Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i0" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i0" onclick="setAnchor('#Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i0')" role="tab">AD_Idmap</a>
    </li><li class="nav-item">
    <a class="nav-link oneOf-option" data-toggle="tab" href="#tab-pane_Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i1" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i1" onclick="setAnchor('#Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i1')" role="tab">LDAP_Idmap</a>
    </li><li class="nav-item">
    <a class="nav-link oneOf-option" data-toggle="tab" href="#tab-pane_Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i2" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i2" onclick="setAnchor('#Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i2')" role="tab">RFC2307_Idmap</a>
    </li><li class="nav-item">
    <a class="nav-link oneOf-option" data-toggle="tab" href="#tab-pane_Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i3" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i3" onclick="setAnchor('#Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i3')" role="tab">RID_Idmap</a>
    </li></ul>
    <div class="tab-content card"><div class="tab-pane fade card-body active show" id="tab-pane_Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i0" role="tabpanel">
    <h4>AD_Idmap</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: object</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>The AD backend reads UID and GID mappings from an Active Directory server that uses pre-existing RFC2307 / SFU     schema extensions. The administrator must add mappings for users and groups in Active Directory before use.</p>
    <p>NOTE: these schema extensions are not present by default in Active Directory.</p>
    </span> <span class="badge badge-info no-additional">No Additional Properties</span>
    <div class="accordion" id="accordionCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i0_name">

    </h2>
    </div>
    <div aria-labelledby="headingCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i0_name" class="collapse property-definition-div" data-parent="#accordionCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i0_name" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i0_name">
    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>Name</h4> <span class="badge badge-success default-value">Default: null</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>Short name for the domain. This should match the NetBIOS domain name for Active Directory domains.     It may be null if the domain is configured as the base idmap for Active Directory. </p>
    </span><div class="any-of-value" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i0_name_anyOf"><h2 class="handle">

    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>Validate Certificates</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: boolean</span> <span class="badge badge-success default-value">Default: true</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>If False, TrueNAS does not validate certificates from the remote LDAP server. It is better to use valid     certificates or import them into the TrueNAS server's trusted certificate store. </p>
    </span>
    </div>

    </div><div class="tab-pane fade card-body" id="tab-pane_Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i3" role="tabpanel">
    <h4>RID_Idmap</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: object</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>The RID backend uses an algorithm to map UIDs and GIDs to SIDs. It determines the UID or GID by adding the RID     value from the Windows Account SID to the base value in range_low. RID values in an Active Directory domain can be     large, especially as the domain ages. Administrators should configure a range large enough to cover the current     RID values assigned by the RID master. One way to do this is to check the RID of a recently created account in     Active Directory. For example, if the RID is 500000, the range must include at least 500000 Unix IDs (for example,     1000000 to 2000000). </p>
    </span> <span class="badge badge-info no-additional">No Additional Properties</span>

    <div class="card-body pl-5">

    <div aria-labelledby="headingCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i3_range_high" class="collapse property-definition-div" data-parent="#accordionCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i3_range_high" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i3_range_high">
    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>Range High</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: integer</span> <span class="badge badge-success default-value">Default: 200000000</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>The highest UID or GID that the idmap backend can assign. </p>
    </span>
    <p><span class="badge badge-light restriction numeric-restriction" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i3_range_high_number">Value must be greater or equal to <code>1000</code> and lesser or equal to <code>2147000000</code></span></p>
    </div>
    </div>
    </div>
    </div>

    <h4>AD_Idmap</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: object</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>The AD backend reads UID and GID mappings from an Active Directory server that uses pre-existing RFC2307 / SFU     schema extensions. The administrator must add mappings for users and groups in Active Directory before use.</p>
    <p>NOTE: these schema extensions are not present by default in Active Directory.</p>
    </span> <span class="badge badge-info no-additional">No Additional Properties</span>

    <div aria-labelledby="headingCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i0_schema_mode" class="collapse property-definition-div" data-parent="#accordionCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i0_schema_mode" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i0_schema_mode">
    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>Schema Mode</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: enum (of string)</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>The schema mode the idmap backend uses to query Active Directory for user and group information. The RFC2307     schema applies to Windows Server 2003 R2 and newer. The Services for Unix (SFU) schema applies to versions before     Windows Server 2003 R2. </p>
    </span><div class="enum-value" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i0_schema_mode_enum">
    <h5>Must be one of:</h5>
    <ul class="list-group"><li class="list-group-item enum-item">"RFC2307"</li><li class="list-group-item enum-item">"SFU"</li><li class="list-group-item enum-item">"SFU20"</li></ul>
    </div>
    </div>
    </div>
    </div>

    </h2>
    </div>
    <div aria-labelledby="headingCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i0_unix_primary_group" class="collapse property-definition-div" data-parent="#accordionCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i0_unix_primary_group" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i0_unix_primary_group">
    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>Unix Primary Group</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: boolean</span> <span class="badge badge-success default-value">Default: false</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>Defines if the user's primary group is fetched from SFU attributes or the Active Directory primary group.     If True, the TrueNAS server uses the <code>gidNumber</code> LDAP attribute. If False, it uses the <code>primaryGroupID</code> LDAP     attribute.</p>
    </span>
    </div>

    <div aria-labelledby="headingCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i0_unix_nss_info" class="collapse property-definition-div" data-parent="#accordionCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i0_unix_nss_info" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i0_unix_nss_info">
    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>Unix Nss Info</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: boolean</span> <span class="badge badge-success default-value">Default: false</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>If True, the login shell and home directory are retrieved from LDAP attributes. If False, or if the Active     Directory LDAP entry lacks SFU attributes, the home directory defaults to <code>/var/empty</code>. </p>

    <h2 class="mb-0">
    <button aria-controls="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i2_validate_certificates" aria-expanded="" class="btn btn-link property-name-button" data-target="#Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i2_validate_certificates" data-toggle="collapse" onclick="setAnchor('#Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i2_validate_certificates')" type="button"><span class="property-name">validate_certificates</span></button>
    </h2>
    </div>
    <div aria-labelledby="headingCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i2_validate_certificates" class="collapse property-definition-div" data-parent="#accordionCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i2_validate_certificates" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i2_validate_certificates">
    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>Validate Certificates</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: boolean</span> <span class="badge badge-success default-value">Default: true</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>If False, TrueNAS does not validate certificates from the remote LDAP server. It is better to use valid     certificates or import them into the TrueNAS server's trusted certificate store. </p>
    </span>
    </div>
    </div>
    </div>

    </div><div class="tab-pane fade card-body" id="tab-pane_Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i3" role="tabpanel">
    <h4>RID_Idmap</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: object</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>The RID backend uses an algorithm to map UIDs and GIDs to SIDs. It determines the UID or GID by adding the RID     value from the Windows Account SID to the base value in range_low. RID values in an Active Directory domain can be     large, especially as the domain ages. Administrators should configure a range large enough to cover the current     RID values assigned by the RID master. One way to do this is to check the RID of a recently created account in     Active Directory. For example, if the RID is 500000, the range must include at least 500000 Unix IDs (for example,     1000000 to 2000000). </p>
    </span> <span class="badge badge-info no-additional">No Additional Properties</span>
    <div class="accordion" id="accordionCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i3_name">

    </h2>
    </div>
    <div aria-labelledby="headingCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i3_range_high" class="collapse property-definition-div" data-parent="#accordionCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i3_range_high" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i3_range_high">
    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>Range High</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: integer</span> <span class="badge badge-success default-value">Default: 200000000</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>The highest UID or GID that the idmap backend can assign. </p>
    </span>
    <p><span class="badge badge-light restriction numeric-restriction" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i3_range_high_number">Value must be greater or equal to <code>1000</code> and lesser or equal to <code>2147000000</code></span></p>
    </div>
    </div>
    </div>
    </div>

    <h4>Validate Certificates</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: boolean</span> <span class="badge badge-success default-value">Default: true</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>If <code>False</code>, TrueNAS does not validate certificates from the remote LDAP server. It is better to use valid     certificates or import them into the TrueNAS server's trusted certificate store. </p>
    </span>
    </div>
    </div>

    <h2 class="mb-0">
    <button aria-controls="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i2_search_bases" aria-expanded="" class="btn btn-link property-name-button" data-target="#Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i2_search_bases" data-toggle="collapse" onclick="setAnchor('#Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i2_search_bases')" type="button"><span class="property-name">search_bases</span></button>
    </h2>
    </div>
    <div aria-labelledby="headingCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i2_search_bases" class="collapse property-definition-div" data-parent="#accordionCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i2_search_bases" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i2_search_bases">
    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>LDAPSearchBases</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: object</span> <div class="json-default-value">Default:<div class="value">{
      "base_user": null,
      "base_group": null,
      "base_netgroup": null
    }</div></div><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>Alternative LDAP search base settings. These settings define where to find user, group, and netgroup entries.     If unspecified (the default), TrueNAS uses the <code>basedn</code> to find users. groups, and netgroups. Use these settings     only if the LDAP server uses a non-standard LDAP schema or if you want to limit the accounts available on     TrueNAS. </p>
    </span> <span class="badge badge-info no-additional">No Additional Properties</span>

    <div class="card">
    <div class="card-header" id="headingCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i2_attribute_maps_shadow">
    <h2 class="mb-0">
    <button aria-controls="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i2_attribute_maps_shadow" aria-expanded="" class="btn btn-link property-name-button" data-target="#Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i2_attribute_maps_shadow" data-toggle="collapse" onclick="setAnchor('#Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i2_attribute_maps_shadow')" type="button"><span class="property-name">shadow</span></button>
    </h2>
    </div>
    <div aria-labelledby="headingCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i2_attribute_maps_shadow" class="collapse property-definition-div" data-parent="#accordionCall_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i2_attribute_maps_shadow" id="Call_parameters_items_i0_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i2_attribute_maps_shadow">
    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>LDAPMapShadow</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: object</span> <div class="json-default-value">Default:<div class="value">{
      "shadow_last_change": null,
      "shadow_min": null,
      "shadow_max": null,
      "shadow_warning": null,
      "shadow_inactive": null,
      "shadow_expire": null

    <div class="accordion" id="accordionReturn_value_credential">
    <div class="card">
    <div class="card-header" id="headingReturn_value_credential">
    <h2 class="mb-0">
    <button aria-controls="Return_value_credential" aria-expanded="" class="btn btn-link property-name-button" data-target="#Return_value_credential" data-toggle="collapse" onclick="setAnchor('#Return_value_credential')" type="button"><span class="property-name">credential</span> <span class="badge badge-warning required-property">Required</span></button>
    </h2>
    </div>
    <div aria-labelledby="headingReturn_value_credential" class="collapse property-definition-div" data-parent="#accordionReturn_value_credential" id="Return_value_credential">
    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>Credential</h4><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>Credential used to bind to the specified directory service. Kerberos credentials are required for Active     Directory or IPA domains. Generic LDAP environments support various authentication methods. Available methods     depend on the remote LDAP server configuration. If Kerberos credentials are selected for LDAP, GSSAPI binds     replace plain LDAP binds. Use Kerberos or mutual TLS authentication when possible for better security.</p>
    <p>The following credential types are supported based on <code>service_type</code>:</p>
    <p><code>ACTIVEDIRECTORY</code> service_type: <code>KERBEROS_USER</code> and <code>KERBEROS_PRINCIPAL</code>.</p>
    <p><code>LDAP</code> service_type: <code>LDAP_PLAIN</code>, <code>LDAP_ANONYMOUS</code>, <code>LDAP_MTLS</code>, <code>KERBEROS_USER</code>, and <code>KERBEROS_PRINCIPAL</code>.     NOTE: prior configuration of kerberos realm is required in order to use kerberos credentials with the <code>LDAP</code> <code>service_type</code>.</p>
    <p><code>IPA</code> service_type: <code>KERBEROS_USER</code> and <code>KERBEROS_PRINCIPAL</code>. NOTE: <code>KERBEROS_USER</code> should be used when initially     joining an IPA domain. </p>
    </span><div class="any-of-value" id="Return_value_credential_anyOf"><h2 class="handle">
    <label>Any of</label>
    </h2><ul class="nav nav-tabs" id="tabsReturn_value_credential_anyOf_anyOf" role="tablist"><li class="nav-item">

    </li><li class="nav-item">
    <a class="nav-link anyOf-option" data-toggle="tab" href="#tab-pane_Return_value_credential_anyOf_i1" id="Return_value_credential_anyOf_i1" onclick="setAnchor('#Return_value_credential_anyOf_i1')" role="tab">Option 2</a>
    </li></ul>

    <h4>Enable</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: boolean</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>Enable the directory service.</p>
    <p>If TrueNAS has never joined the specified domain (IPA or Active Directory), setting this to True causes TrueNAS to     attempt to join the domain.</p>
    <p>NOTE: The domain join process for Active Directory and IPA will make changes to the domain such as creating a new     computer account for the TrueNAS server and creating DNS records for TrueNAS. </p>
    </span>

    <div class="accordion" id="accordionReturn_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain">
    <div class="card">
    <div class="card-header" id="headingReturn_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain">
    <h2 class="mb-0">
    <button aria-controls="Return_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain" aria-expanded="" class="btn btn-link property-name-button" data-target="#Return_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain" data-toggle="collapse" onclick="setAnchor('#Return_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain')" type="button"><span class="property-name">idmap_domain</span></button>
    </h2>
    </div>
    <div aria-labelledby="headingReturn_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain" class="collapse property-definition-div" data-parent="#accordionReturn_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain" id="Return_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain">
    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>Idmap Domain</h4> <div class="json-default-value">Default:<div class="value">{
      "name": null,
      "range_low": 100000001,
      "range_high": 200000000,
      "idmap_backend": "RID",
      "sssd_compat": false
    }</div></div><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>This configuration defines how domain accounts joined to TrueNAS are mapped to Unix UIDs and GIDs on the     TrueNAS server. Most TrueNAS deployments use the RID backend, which algorithmically assigns UIDs and GIDs based on     the Active Directory account SID. Another common option is the AD backend, which reads predefined Active Directory     LDAP schema attributes that assign explicit UID and GID numbers to accounts. </p>
    </span><div class="one-of-value" id="Return_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf"><h2 class="handle">
    <label>One of</label>
    </h2><ul class="nav nav-tabs" id="tabsReturn_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_oneOf" role="tablist"><li class="nav-item">
    <a class="nav-link active oneOf-option" data-toggle="tab" href="#tab-pane_Return_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i0" id="Return_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i0" onclick="setAnchor('#Return_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i0')" role="tab">AD_Idmap</a>
    </li><li class="nav-item">

    <div class="tab-content card"><div class="tab-pane fade card-body active show" id="tab-pane_Return_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i0" role="tabpanel">
    <h4>AD_Idmap</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: object</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>The AD backend reads UID and GID mappings from an Active Directory server that uses pre-existing RFC2307 / SFU     schema extensions. The administrator must add mappings for users and groups in Active Directory before use.</p>
    <p>NOTE: these schema extensions are not present by default in Active Directory.</p>
    </span> <span class="badge badge-info no-additional">No Additional Properties</span>

    <div aria-labelledby="headingReturn_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i2_validate_certificates" class="collapse property-definition-div" data-parent="#accordionReturn_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i2_validate_certificates" id="Return_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i2_validate_certificates">
    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>Validate Certificates</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: boolean</span> <span class="badge badge-success default-value">Default: true</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>If False, TrueNAS does not validate certificates from the remote LDAP server. It is better to use valid     certificates or import them into the TrueNAS server's trusted certificate store. </p>
    </span>
    </div>

    </div><div class="tab-pane fade card-body" id="tab-pane_Return_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i3" role="tabpanel">
    <h4>RID_Idmap</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: object</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>The RID backend uses an algorithm to map UIDs and GIDs to SIDs. It determines the UID or GID by adding the RID     value from the Windows Account SID to the base value in range_low. RID values in an Active Directory domain can be     large, especially as the domain ages. Administrators should configure a range large enough to cover the current     RID values assigned by the RID master. One way to do this is to check the RID of a recently created account in     Active Directory. For example, if the RID is 500000, the range must include at least 500000 Unix IDs (for example,     1000000 to 2000000). </p>
    </span> <span class="badge badge-info no-additional">No Additional Properties</span>

    <span class="description"><p>The highest UID or GID that the idmap backend can assign. </p>

    <p><span class="badge badge-light restriction numeric-restriction" id="Return_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_idmap_idmap_domain_oneOf_i3_range_high_number">Value must be greater or equal to <code>1000</code> and lesser or equal to <code>2147000000</code></span></p>

    <h2 class="mb-0">
    <button aria-controls="Return_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i2_validate_certificates" aria-expanded="" class="btn btn-link property-name-button" data-target="#Return_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i2_validate_certificates" data-toggle="collapse" onclick="setAnchor('#Return_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i2_validate_certificates')" type="button"><span class="property-name">validate_certificates</span></button>
    </h2>
    </div>
    <div aria-labelledby="headingReturn_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i2_validate_certificates" class="collapse property-definition-div" data-parent="#accordionReturn_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i2_validate_certificates" id="Return_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i2_validate_certificates">
    <div class="card-body pl-5">
    <h4>Validate Certificates</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: boolean</span> <span class="badge badge-success default-value">Default: true</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>If False, TrueNAS does not validate certificates from the remote LDAP server. It is better to use valid     certificates or import them into the TrueNAS server's trusted certificate store. </p>
    </span>
    </div>
    </div>
    </div>
    </div>
    </div><div class="tab-pane fade card-body" id="tab-pane_Return_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i3" role="tabpanel">
    <h4>RID_Idmap</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: object</span><br/>
    <span class="description"><p>The RID backend uses an algorithm to map UIDs and GIDs to SIDs. It determines the UID or GID by adding the RID     value from the Windows Account SID to the base value in range_low. RID values in an Active Directory domain can be     large, especially as the domain ages. Administrators should configure a range large enough to cover the current     RID values assigned by the RID master. One way to do this is to check the RID of a recently created account in     Active Directory. For example, if the RID is 500000, the range must include at least 500000 Unix IDs (for example,     1000000 to 2000000). </p>
    </span> <span class="badge badge-info no-additional">No Additional Properties</span>
    <div class="accordion" id="accordionReturn_value_configuration_anyOf_i0_oneOf_i0_trusted_domains_items_oneOf_i3_name">

    <h4>IPAConfig</h4><span class="badge badge-dark value-type">Type: object</span><br/>
    <span class="badge badge-info no-additional">No Additional Properties</span>
